  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_19cdd440-7cbd-48c7-b3ef-e723eb919af7'
      });

<div id="review_1932080578" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1932080578" />
    <a title="Natalie Vellacott" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/34178791-natalie-vellacott"><img alt="Natalie Vellacott" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442984500p2/34178791.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1932080578?book_show_action=true">Mar 07, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Natalie Vellacott" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Natalie Vellacott" href="/user/show/34178791-natalie-vellacott">Natalie Vellacott</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781414349763" href="/book/show/11326693-fame">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34178791-natalie-vellacott?shelf=christian-fiction">christian-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1932080578" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6360162923415082428">This was my first Karen Kingsbury book and honestly it was just okay. I probably wouldn't bother to read the rest of this series as it just didn't hold my interest.<br/><br/>The main character is offered a big break in a Hollywood film. She is living in a quiet rural community and was apparently headhunted by a male movie star due to her appearance of innocence. She auditions and perhaps not surprisingly is offered the part...I won't spoil the rest of the story but it revolves around faith vs fame choices</span>
  <span id="freeText6360162923415082428" style="display:none">This was my first Karen Kingsbury book and honestly it was just okay. I probably wouldn't bother to read the rest of this series as it just didn't hold my interest.<br /><br />The main character is offered a big break in a Hollywood film. She is living in a quiet rural community and was apparently headhunted by a male movie star due to her appearance of innocence. She auditions and perhaps not surprisingly is offered the part...I won't spoil the rest of the story but it revolves around faith vs fame choices.<br /><br />The storyline was a little unrealistic especially due to the fact that the main character had been involved in film in the past but had walked away due to a personal crisis. What are the chances that she would be headhunted by this man who knew nothing of her background?<br /><br />I liked the way the author tried to demonstrate the dangers of power/money/fame within Hollywood and how this can corrupt a person. But, I would have liked to read more references to the faith of the main character. She felt God checking her on a number of occasions but proceeded anyway due to being caught up in the excitement. This was a more realistic scenario and something we all need to be aware of--just because it seems to be right, doesn't mean it is. We should proceed with caution and take advice from others.<br /><br />There was no bad language in this book but there were some bedroom scenes that had a little too much detail and there is a violent scene which is quite graphic.<br /><br />I wouldn't really recommend this book--it was too predictable with not enough of a Christian message.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6360162923415082428" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer9247506336140554704">My heart always feels light and at peace after reading a Karen Kingsbury book. She’s my favorite for a reason and it’s because her words, her characters, and her storylines always resonate deep within me. They’ll teach you life lessons that you’ll carry with you forever...   <span id="freeText9247506336140554704" style="display:none">My heart always feels light and at peace after reading a Karen Kingsbury book. She’s my favorite for a reason and it’s because her words, her characters, and her storylines always resonate deep within me. They’ll teach you life lessons that you’ll carry with you forever... I can promise you that.<br />Fame is book one of the Firstborn series and I absolutely loved it. Getting to know Dayne Matthews at a deeper level after his brief appearance in the series before this one was a nice treat. You also get to know and befriend Katy Hart and of course dive right back into the heart of the Baxter family. I can’t get enough of the Baxter family and I can’t wait to continue reading this series.<br />Karen Kingsbury, thank you for sharing stories from your heart and for giving readers like me a lighthearted peace after reading each of your books.</span>

  <span id="freeText9898520556678315805" style="display:none">Okay, this book is really good. I really LOVE the writing style. Other than the falling in love part, I never once went, "This is going too fast." unlike other books that I've read. Plus, the author's writing styles really...Ah, I can't even explain it, but it brings life, and a bit of peppyness that really attracted me. <br />The whole storyline of a nobody with a celebirty falling for her is cliche, but the author really did her job in making it interesting. Even though the author didn't want Katy to stay in Hollywood, I wish she was in hollywood longer ^^<br />However, there are things I would like to change. Such as the baxters. I haven't read the redemption series yet, but when I read fame, I was awefully confused. The baxters in this series did almost nothing. I wish they had more interations with the two main characters rather than just living their own life. <br />This story was cheesy, but I love cheesy, so it's okay. The names seemed perfect for each other, as if I could really imagine meeting a girl named Katy Hart at church, and seeing a movie star named Dane Matthews. Heck, even Sarah Jo is a perfect name since Sarah Jo is trying to be Mary Sue.<br />I loves this book, I really did, and I can't wait to read the other things that the author has written (Once I have money of course)</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer212428044" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3738151080779308949">My mom talked me into reading these books (yes, all of them) because they take place in Bloomington, Indiana. I, however, didn't realize that Bloomington, Indiana was Christian paradise, or at least it was depicted so in these books which more closely resemble an evangelical soap opera. Karen Kingsbury seems to subscribe to rather bipolar theology where terrible things happen to every single character in the books (murder, suicide, terminal illness, abortion, etc.), but luckily they pray about i</span>
  <span id="freeText3738151080779308949" style="display:none">My mom talked me into reading these books (yes, all of them) because they take place in Bloomington, Indiana. I, however, didn't realize that Bloomington, Indiana was Christian paradise, or at least it was depicted so in these books which more closely resemble an evangelical soap opera. Karen Kingsbury seems to subscribe to rather bipolar theology where terrible things happen to every single character in the books (murder, suicide, terminal illness, abortion, etc.), but luckily they pray about it and live happily ever after. Two women in the books are married to pro football players, and one marries America's favorite movie star, because that's what happens to everyone, right? I think these books have gone way past "fiction enough to be enjoyable" to " Christianized harlequin romance novels for discontent middle aged women."<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3738151080779308949" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer11843640289843935124">I would actually give about 3 1/2 stars. Karen Kingsbury is really good at what she does, which is cheesy Christian fiction with a little bit of romance thrown in. It's very "sweet", and at times a little too much. I'm sure there are people out there like these characters, but I don't know any.<br/><br/>But the writing flows smoothly, and is a style that is easy to read. I liked the book, and was left wanting to read the next in the series at the end. I would definitely read the Redemption series before t</span>
  <span id="freeText11843640289843935124" style="display:none">I would actually give about 3 1/2 stars. Karen Kingsbury is really good at what she does, which is cheesy Christian fiction with a little bit of romance thrown in. It's very "sweet", and at times a little too much. I'm sure there are people out there like these characters, but I don't know any.<br /><br />But the writing flows smoothly, and is a style that is easy to read. I liked the book, and was left wanting to read the next in the series at the end. I would definitely read the Redemption series before this one, though, because this book constantly refers to things that happened there, and I think you'd feel a little lost and wouldn't be able to connect with or care about most of the characters.</span>

<div id="review_295828085" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/295828085" />
    <a title="Tamara Tilley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1383724-tamara-tilley"><img alt="Tamara Tilley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1224873451p2/1383724.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/295828085?book_show_action=true">Mar 17, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tamara Tilley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tamara Tilley" href="/user/show/1383724-tamara-tilley">Tamara Tilley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1383724-tamara-tilley?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1383724-tamara-tilley?shelf=karen-kingsbury">karen-kingsbury</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer295828085" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2562715358763169031">FAME is the first book in the Firstborn series, which follows the Redemption series by Karen Kingsbury.<br/><br/>Dayne Matthews, Hollywood heartthrob, whom we briefly met in REUNION, is captivated by Katy Hart. Katy is a director of children’s theater that Dayne stumbled across while he was in Bloomington, Indiana. Though their meeting was brief and one-sided, for whatever reason he can’t seem to get her out of his mind. When he returns to Hollywood and is cast in a new romantic comedy, the only woman he </span>
  <span id="freeText2562715358763169031" style="display:none">FAME is the first book in the Firstborn series, which follows the Redemption series by Karen Kingsbury.<br /><br />Dayne Matthews, Hollywood heartthrob, whom we briefly met in REUNION, is captivated by Katy Hart. Katy is a director of children’s theater that Dayne stumbled across while he was in Bloomington, Indiana. Though their meeting was brief and one-sided, for whatever reason he can’t seem to get her out of his mind. When he returns to Hollywood and is cast in a new romantic comedy, the only woman he can picture to play his leading lady is Katy. After digging into her background, and finding out she was once an actress before a director of children’s theater, he convinces the casting director to give her a call. Dayne’s infatuation with Katy is of overwhelming proportions. His mind wanders constantly about how it would be if they became more than co-stars. His fear–the Hollywood lifestyle will scare her off, and the down home, wholesome, Katy will never be able to see past his tabloid, playboy image. <br /><br />Katy Hart cannot believe what is happening to her. One day she is casting the roles for her children’s theater, and the next, she is being contacted by a Hollywood casting director wanting her to test for an upcoming movie starring none other than Dayne Matthews, Hollywood’s own Don Juan. Though she is convinced it is some kind of joke or a mistake, Katy follows agrees to fly to Hollywood to do a reading. The electricity she feels with Dayne Matthews is immediate. And soon, Katy feels the struggle of wanting to reach for her dream, and the fear of being drawn into a lifestyle diametrically opposed to her conservative values.<br /><br />I could not wait to read FAME. I’ve had it since its original release in 2005 but never found the time to read it. When the series, starting with the Redemption series from Karen Kingsbury continued to expand, I fell further behind. So, it was with much anticipation I began to read. Sometimes that kind of anticipation leaves you wanting. I would not say I was disappointed, but I did find myself breezing over some of the longer sections written from the authorial view, and would speed through the sections that did not center on Katy and Dayne. Ms. Kingsbury took her time in developing the story between Katy and Dayne, but all too soon, it came to an abrupt end. I was a little disappointed with the ending, feeling as if too many frayed ends were left exposed. I can only hope that FORGIVEN, the second book in the series, ties up some of those ends without it becoming more drawn out. I am all for suspense, and leaving the reader dangling, but not so much when the filler used to extend the story is not as intriguing.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2562715358763169031" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1105500684" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1105500684" />
    <a title="Bekah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25766853-bekah"><img alt="Bekah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1556065407p2/25766853.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bekah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bekah" href="/user/show/25766853-bekah">Bekah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/16102925-fame">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25766853-bekah?shelf=books-read-in-2014">books-read-in-2014</a>,

          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1105500684" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1225607928083380428">I really loved this book. I loved how <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3159984.Karen_Kingsbury' title='Karen Kingsbury' rel='nofollow noopener'>Karen Kingsbury</a> added in the Baxter family in this book, but mainly focused on Dayne and Katy. <br/><br/>Katy Hart is the young director of CKT (Christian Kid's Theater) and loves what she does. But for as long as she could remember, her dream was to be an actress and when an unexpected offer comes up from a Hollywood casting director, she makes the decision to head up to CA for an audition. But above all, she wants what God wants for her. Is it in His plan for her li</span>
  <span id="freeText1225607928083380428" style="display:none">I really loved this book. I loved how <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3159984.Karen_Kingsbury" title="Karen Kingsbury" rel="nofollow noopener">Karen Kingsbury</a> added in the Baxter family in this book, but mainly focused on Dayne and Katy. <br /><br />Katy Hart is the young director of CKT (Christian Kid's Theater) and loves what she does. But for as long as she could remember, her dream was to be an actress and when an unexpected offer comes up from a Hollywood casting director, she makes the decision to head up to CA for an audition. But above all, she wants what God wants for her. Is it in His plan for her life to be the lead female actor in this upcoming movie? Or is God leading her in another direction?<br /><br />Dayne Matthews, a famous actor, has had a grudge against God ever since he was a teenager and wants nothing to do with Him. After what happened a year ago after finding his biological mother, he comes to realize even more what his fame has cost him.<br /><br />I really loved this story. What was SO refreshing was to see Katy's strong convictions and how she stood by them. She valued purity and wanted to make sure that whatever she did was pleasing to the Lord. Yes, she did make mistakes, but it was so awesome to read of her trying her utmost to be pleasing to the Lord.<br /><br />I can't wait to begin the second book in this series--<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11434.Forgiven__Firstborn___2_" title="Forgiven (Firstborn, #2) by Karen Kingsbury" rel="nofollow noopener">Forgiven</a>. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1225607928083380428" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3480373504" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3480373504" />
    <a title="Jack Vasen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52966326-jack-vasen"><img alt="Jack Vasen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1456179595p2/52966326.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3480373504?book_show_action=true">Aug 05, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jack Vasen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jack Vasen" href="/user/show/52966326-jack-vasen">Jack Vasen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52966326-jack-vasen?shelf=christian">christian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52966326-jack-vasen?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52966326-jack-vasen?shelf=series-must-read-all">series-must-read-all</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3480373504" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4916858807765068897">This series is mostly one long story which is built upon characters developed in a previous series (The Redemption Collection). This first book almost tells a complete story but there are such obvious unresolved threads that finishing this book alone is unsatisfying. This is definitely a series to be read in order. As to characters from the previous series, the author fills us in on the important details, but as I was reading, I definitely realized I was missing something since I had not read th</span>
  <span id="freeText4916858807765068897" style="display:none">This series is mostly one long story which is built upon characters developed in a previous series (The Redemption Collection). This first book almost tells a complete story but there are such obvious unresolved threads that finishing this book alone is unsatisfying. This is definitely a series to be read in order. As to characters from the previous series, the author fills us in on the important details, but as I was reading, I definitely realized I was missing something since I had not read the earlier books. I wish publishers would make these things more apparent before you pick up a book and find you are investing in a continuing saga, or find you are missing some background.<br /><br />There are many important characters in this story. If you have not grown with them in the earlier series, it is a bit difficult to keep up with them all at first. The story is rich in the sense of being full of plot threads to follow.<br /><br />For a while there is a bit of a Cinderella flavor as Katy has her shot at the big time and enjoys the thrills that come with that. One of the plot threads is watching Katy try to retain her Godly values while being confronted with a world well known for how it corrupts those in it. She has already experienced some of that in her backstory. (I don't know if her backstory is covered in an earlier book, but based on the way it is slowly revealed in this one, I would guess not.)<br /><br />Dayne also has a backstory some of which I suspect is covered in the earlier series. He will be a central figure in this book and the rest of the series. He has both good and bad qualities and it's easy to guess that much of the series will be aimed at redeeming him from the bad ones.<br /><br />I don't know how accurate the background atmosphere is, but the author paints the struggles of celebrities maintaining their privacy as pretty much a hopeless one.<br /><br />This is a Christian book, as anyone who is familiar with Kingsbury knows. Characters frequently pray and depend on God for guidance. God even speaks inaudibly to some at times. There's not much preaching in actual speeches, but the topic of trusting God is definitely front and center.<br /><br />Mature themes: clearly several characters are leading lives that involve sex and drugs and parties. Yet sex is never described at all other than to indicate that it happens. There is a crazy knife carrying stalker. <br /><br />Star rating: the continuing nature of the series and unresolved threads is a pet peeve of mine, especially in longer series. It happens that when I picked this up, I didn't have time to complete 5 books without an extended break in between at some point. I am sorely tempted to give this book 1 star because an incomplete story is not worthy of more. However, it is a story with definite possibilities and it is excellent as far as it goes. Weight 5 stars with 1 star = 3 stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4916858807765068897" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer3142427984309081089">This book was a great start to the First Born series. This book obviously focused on the first born son of the Baxter family, Dayne Matthews. Dayne is a successful Hollywood actor, trying to cast a lead role to play opposite him in his next movie, a romantic comedy. None of the top Hollywood actresses seem to fit the part because it calls for an innocent small town girl. But Dayne thinks he knows who would be perfect...Katy Hart, the girl who runs the Children’s Christian Theater. He saw her at </span>
  <span id="freeText3142427984309081089" style="display:none">This book was a great start to the First Born series. This book obviously focused on the first born son of the Baxter family, Dayne Matthews. Dayne is a successful Hollywood actor, trying to cast a lead role to play opposite him in his next movie, a romantic comedy. None of the top Hollywood actresses seem to fit the part because it calls for an innocent small town girl. But Dayne thinks he knows who would be perfect...Katy Hart, the girl who runs the Children’s Christian Theater. He saw her at the theater last year when he went inside after a trip to visit his biological mother, Elizabeth Baxter, when she was dying in the hospital. The director is able to get in touch with Katy, and she goes to try out for the part. She even goes a second time to try out a scene with Dayne. She’s perfect for the part. Katy and Dayne get to know each other, and spend time in places where hopefully the paparazzi won’t see Dayne. Unfortunately, the paparazzi aren’t the only people that Dayne needs to worry about...a crazy fan with multiple personalities is also stalking Dayne, to the point where she thinks they’re married and she has to kill any woman that is with Dayne. When Katy is sure she is ready to give up her life in Bloomington and take the movie role, the crazy woman comes to the secluded beach where Dayne and Katy were having dinner and tries to kill Katy with a knife. Even though Dayne manages to get the woman away from Katy, and the police come, Katy knows she can’t make this movie with Dayne. Her life is working at the children’s theater helping to put on the next play, Tom Sawyer. She goes back to Bloomington to a successful opening night. We’re left wondering...what will happen to Dayne and Katy’s relationship? Dayne isn’t happy with his relationship with actress Kelly Parker. And will he ever be reunited with his biological family, the Baxter’s? <br />John Baxter is slowly getting back to life without Elizabeth. He’s determined not to bring up the past that the first born of the family was a son he and Elizabeth gave away. With Ashley finding old letters of her parents, the secret almost was revealed. <br />Brooke’s daughter Hayley is still improving from her drowning accident. <br />Kari, Ryan, Ashley, and Landon help out the CKT Theater with painting sets. Ashley and Landon are able to take their honeymoon now that things are settled down at home. <br />Luke and Regan are adopting a baby. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3142427984309081089" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melanie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melanie" href="/user/show/9834339-melanie">Melanie</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1567070548" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5209805177801852597">Fame is the sixth book in the Baxter series and the first book in the Firstborn series. <br/><br/>Danye Matthews is starring in a new movie role and needs an innocent looking woman to be his co-star. His first thought is Katy Hart. She is the director of the CKT, Christian Kids Theater. Danye saw Katy in the book Reunion for a few minutes and was instantly drawn to her. Mitch Henry is the casting director for the new movie. Danye wants Mitch to find Katy and get there for an audition. Katy is in Bloomingt</span>
  <span id="freeText5209805177801852597" style="display:none">Fame is the sixth book in the Baxter series and the first book in the Firstborn series. <br /><br />Danye Matthews is starring in a new movie role and needs an innocent looking woman to be his co-star. His first thought is Katy Hart. She is the director of the CKT, Christian Kids Theater. Danye saw Katy in the book Reunion for a few minutes and was instantly drawn to her. Mitch Henry is the casting director for the new movie. Danye wants Mitch to find Katy and get there for an audition. Katy is in Bloomington, IN working on the newest production for the kids, Tom Sawyer. Katy left the Hollywood life behind her for personal reasons many years before. She is happy being the director at CKT and working with the kids. When the phone call from Mitch to come to Hollywood and audition for a movie with Danye Matthews, Katy thinks it is a joke. That is until she gets out to Hollywood and finds out that Mitch is the real deal and Danye Matthews is standing in front of her talking to her about the scene. Katy is in Bloomington on the CKT production and going back and forth to Hollywood to do another audition and then to tell Danye her answer on whether she will take the part or not. <br /><br />Chloe has a multiple personality with another personality being Anna, her sister. Chloe thinks she is married to Danye and she has plans to kill any woman that comes between her and Danye. Katy happened to be with Danye and is attacked when Chloe jumps out of the bushes and grabs her.<br /><br />Kelly Parker is being hounded by the paparazzi to the point where she is afraid to leave her house. Kelly has an on again, off again relationship with Danye but she wants more. Kelly auditions for the party that Katy is in line for but Danye knows that Katy is the definite one for it.<br /><br />I love how Karen has started a whole new series with a new list of characters but is able to bring the Baxters into this book as well. John is still trying to hide the fact that they have a firstborn son. Ashley, Kari, Ryan and Landon all help with the panting of the set for Tom Sawyer. The Baxters are still having a family get together as well. I really enjoyed this book and I can't wait to start Forgiven.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5209805177801852597" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer2814859586131580958">I remember now why I quit reading Karen Kingsbury. Her books are structurally well-written, and her character-development is thorough; but I prefer my Christian fiction "morals" to be a little more realistic and subtle than her characters usually depict. I also do not like for an author to write dialogue for God. I listened to this audiobook while I walked for exercise, and it was interesting enough to keep me walking. The actress who read the novel did not do the book justice, either. Every fem</span>
  <span id="freeText2814859586131580958" style="display:none">I remember now why I quit reading Karen Kingsbury. Her books are structurally well-written, and her character-development is thorough; but I prefer my Christian fiction "morals" to be a little more realistic and subtle than her characters usually depict. I also do not like for an author to write dialogue for God. I listened to this audiobook while I walked for exercise, and it was interesting enough to keep me walking. The actress who read the novel did not do the book justice, either. Every female character sounded like a naive 10-year-old. That got nerve-wracking a few chapters into the book. </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2060917171" />
    <a title="Donna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/925762-donna"><img alt="Donna" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Donna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Donna" href="/user/show/925762-donna">Donna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2060917171" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2001623709765031410">I was really thrown off by the name change of Jamie Hart to Katy Hart. Apparently that was the publisher's decision, as the author had used the name Jamie in another unrelated series. It didn't make any sense to me. The author started using the new name towards the end of "Reunion" where Dayne is trying to remember her name. Katy is the name he came up with. At the time I thought he had remembered it wrong.<br/>The story was pretty good although not as intense as the books from the Redemption series.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('QtISx16OJErB5f8JQS8ccbwNsfrf0sZbPWeNjmlN8mkbLVG7RZDd8APosIznUko8vfmI8/i+ZGb/ncxEKjX79w==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('W6BVuZTajaaGifvwfIxrUKpWfEA8nJbnlJDpiSDjbVQCXxbFj8R0HESEtHXa8T0dq6JFSRvwNNpWaqhDY5tkyg==')})
  }

After surviving the massacre of her family and the destruction of Jerusalem by the Romans, Hadassah is captured and sold to a well-to-do merchant’s family. Hadassah struggles to walk in the footsteps of Jesus and to treat her masters in a manner in keeping with His teachings, but she is forced to keep her religious identity a secret in order to survive. Confused and alone, she has only her faith to cling to as she tries to subtly bring God into the lives of her captors. Reckless, impulsive, and villainous, Julia tries to undermine Hadassah at every turn. But Julia’s brother, Marcus, is a different sort altogether. Is it possible for a love between Hadassah and Marcus to flourish considering not only their differing stations in life, but also the gap between Hadassah’s unrelenting faith and Marcus’ lack of belief in anything? Simultaneously, Atretes, a captured soldier from Germania, is forced to become a gladiator.   <span id="freeText10545747271857172927" style="display:none">Karen Kingsbury, #1 New York Times bestselling novelist, is America’s favorite inspirational storyteller, with more than twenty-five million copies of her award-winning books in print. Her last dozen titles have topped bestseller lists and many of her novels are under development with Hallmark Films and as major motion pictures. Her Baxter Family books are being developed into a TV series slated for major network viewing sometime in the next year. Karen is also an adjunct professor of writing at Liberty University. In 2001 she and her husband, Don, adopted three boys from Haiti, doubling their family in a matter of months.
